title="UTC+1">UTC+1</a> (CET)</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><span style="white-space:nowrap">&#160;\xe2\x80\xa2&#160;Summer (<a href="/wiki/Daylight_saving_time" title="Daylight 3166">ISO 3166 code</a></th><td class="nickname">\nFR-E</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Brittany</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/\xc9\xaa/: &#39;i&#39; in &#39;kit&#39;">\xc9\xaa</span><span title="&#39;t&#39; in &#39;tie&#39;">t</span><span title="/\xc9\x99n/: &#39;on&#39; in &#39;button&#39;">\xc9\x99n</span><span title="/i/: &#39;y&#39; in &#39;happy&#39;">i</span></span>/</a></span></span>; French: <i lang="fr">Bretagne</i> <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[b\xca\x81\xc9\x99ta\xc9\xb2]</a></span><small class="nowrap">&#160;(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Fr-Bretagne.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20" /></a>&#160;</span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/1/1b/Fr-Bretagne.ogg" class="internal" title="Fr-Bretagne.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</small>; <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a>: <i lang="br">Breizh</i>, pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Breton" title="Help:IPA/Breton">[b\xca\x81\xc9\x9bjs]</a></span> or <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Breton" title="Help:IPA/Breton">[b\xca\x81\xc9\x9b\xcf\x87]</a></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-Walter_1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walter-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gallo_language" title="Gallo language">Gallo</a>: <i>Berta\xc3\xa8yn</i>, pronounced <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/French" title="Help:IPA/French">[b\xc9\x99\xca\x81ta\xc9\x9b\xc9\xb2]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Cultural_region" class="mw-redirect" title="Cultural region">cultural region</a> in the northwest of <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, covering the western part of what was known as <a href="/wiki/Armorica" title="Armorica">Armorica</a> during the period of Roman occupation. It became an <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Brittany" title="Kingdom of Brittany">independent kingdom</a> and then a <a href="/wiki/Duchy_of_Brittany" title="Duchy of Brittany">duchy</a> before being <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Brittany_and_France" title="Union of Brittany and France">united</a> with the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Kingdom of France</a> in 1532 as a <a href="/wiki/Provinces_of_France" title="Provinces of France">province</a> governed as if it were a separate nation under the crown.\n</p><p>Brittany has also been referred to as <i>Less</i>, <i>Lesser</i> or <i>Little</i> Britain (as opposed to <i><a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a></i>, with which it shares an etymology).<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> It is bordered by the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> to the north, the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Sea" title="Celtic Sea">Celtic Sea</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a> to the west, and the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Biscay" title="Bay of Biscay">Bay of Biscay</a> to the south. Its land area is 34,023&#160;km\xc2\xb2 <span class="nowrap">(13,136 sq mi)</span>.\n</p><p>Brittany is the site of some of the world\'s oldest standing architecture, home to the <a href="/wiki/Barnenez" title="Barnenez">Barnenez</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tumulus_Saint-Michel" class="mw-redirect" title="Tumulus Saint-Michel">Tumulus Saint-Michel</a> and others, which date to the early 5th millennium BC.<sup id="cite_ref-Saint-Michel_tumulus_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Saint-Michel_tumulus-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Today, the historical province of Brittany is split among five French departments: <a href="/wiki/Finist%C3%A8re" title="Finist\xc3\xa8re">Finist\xc3\xa8re</a> in the west, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4tes-d%27Armor" title="C\xc3\xb4tes-d&#39;Armor">C\xc3\xb4tes-d\'Armor</a> in the north, <a href="/wiki/Ille-et-Vilaine" title="Ille-et-Vilaine">Ille-et-Vilaine</a> in the north east, <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">Loire-Atlantique</a> in the south east and <a href="/wiki/Morbihan" title="Morbihan">Morbihan</a> in the south on the Bay of Biscay. Since reorganisation in 1956, the modern <a href="/wiki/Brittany_(administrative_region)" title="Brittany (administrative region)">administrative region of Brittany</a> comprises only four of the five Breton departments, or 80% of historical Brittany. The remaining area of old Brittany, the Loire-Atlantique department around <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, now forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Pays_de_la_Loire" title="Pays de la Loire">Pays de la Loire</a> region.\n</p><p>At the 2010 census, the population of historic Brittany was estimated to be 4,475,295. Of these, 71% lived in the region of Brittany, while 29% lived in the Loire-Atlantique department. In 2012, the largest metropolitan areas were <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a> (897,713 inhabitants), <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a> (690,467 inhabitants), and <a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest</a> (314,844 inhabitants).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Brittany is the traditional homeland of the <a href="/wiki/Bretons" title="Bretons">Breton people</a> and is recognised by the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_League" title="Celtic League">Celtic League</a> as one of the six <a href="/wiki/Celtic_nations" title="Celtic nations">Celtic nations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> retaining a distinct <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Brittany" title="Culture of Brittany">cultural identity</a> that reflects its <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brittany" title="History of Brittany">history</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Breton_nationalism" title="Breton nationalism">nationalist movement</a> seeks greater autonomy within the French Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 class="toclevel-2 tocsection-25"><a href="#Regional_identity"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Regional identity</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-26"><a class="tocnumber">7.2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Breton</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-28"><a href="#Gallo"><span class="tocnumber">7.2.2</span> <span class="toctext">Religion</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-30"><a href="#Culture"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Culture</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-31"><a href="#Architecture"><span class="tocnumber">8.1</span> <span class="toctext">Architecture</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-32"><a literature</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-35"><a href="#Museums"><span class="tocnumber">8.5</span> <span class="toctext">Museums</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Festivals"><span class="tocnumber">8.6</span> <span class="toctext">Festivals</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Sport"><span class="tocnumber">8.7</span> <span class="toctext">Sport</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Cuisine"><span class="tocnumber">8.8</span> <span class="toctext">Cuisine</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Transport"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Transport</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Road"><span class="tocnumber">9.1</span> <span class="toctext">Road</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Air"><span class="tocnumber">9.2</span> <span class="toctext">Air</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42"><a href="#Rail"><span class="tocnumber">9.3</span> <span tocsection-44"><a href="#Cycling"><span class="tocnumber">9.5</span> <span class="toctext">Cycling</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#Symbols"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Symbols</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Image_gallery"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Image gallery</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-49"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The word <i>Brittany</i>, along with its <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gallo_language" title="Gallo language">Gallo</a> equivalents <i>Bretagne</i>, <i>Breizh</i> and <i>Berta\xc3\xa8yn</i>, derive from the <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Britannia" title="Britannia">Britannia</a></i>, which means "<a href="/wiki/Britons_(Celtic_people)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (Celtic people)">Britons</a>\' land". This word had been used by the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a> since the 1st century to refer to Great Britain, and more specifically the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Britain" title="Roman Britain">Roman province of Britain</a>. This word derives from a <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Ancient Greek language">Greek</a> word, \xce\xa0\xcf\x81\xce\xb5\xcf\x84\xcf\x84\xce\xb1\xce\xbd\xce\xb9\xce\xba\xce\xb7 (Prettanike) or \xce\x92\xcf\x81\xce\xb5\xcf\x84\xcf\x84\xce\xb1\xce\xbd\xce\xaf\xce\xb1\xce\xb9 (Brettaniai), used by <a href="/wiki/Pytheas" title="Pytheas">Pytheas</a>, an explorer from <a href="/wiki/Marseille" title="Marseille">Massalia</a> who visited the <a href="/wiki/British_Islands" title="British Islands">British Islands</a> around 320 BC. The Greek word itself comes from the common Brythonic ethnonym reconstructed as *Pritani, itself from Proto-Celtic \'*K\xca\xb7ritan\xc4\xab from Proto-Indo-European <a class="external text" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Indo-European/k%CA%B7er-">*k\xca\xb7er</a> \' to do.\nThe Romans called Brittany <i><a href="/wiki/Armorica" title="Armorica">Armorica</a></i>, together with a quite indefinite region that extended along the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> coast from the <a href="/wiki/Seine" title="Seine">Seine</a> estuary to the <a href="/wiki/Loire" title="Loire">Loire</a> estuary, and according to several sources, maybe along the Atlantic coast to the <a href="/wiki/Garonne" title="Garonne">Garonne</a> estuary. This term probably comes from a <a href="/wiki/Gallic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Gallic language">Gallic</a> word, <i>aremorica</i>, which means "close to the sea".<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Another name, <i>Letauia</i> (in English "<a href="/wiki/Litavis" title="Litavis">Litavis</a>"), was used until the 12th century. It possibly means "wide and flat" or "to expand" and it gave the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> name for Brittany: <i>Llydaw</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After the fall of the <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">Western Roman Empire</a>, many <a href="/wiki/Britons" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons">Britons</a> settled in western Armorica, and the region started to be called <i>Britannia</i>, although this name only replaced <i>Armorica</i> in the sixth century or perhaps by the end of the fifth.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> Later, authors like <a href="/wiki/Geoffrey_of_Monmouth" title="Geoffrey of Monmouth">Geoffrey of Monmouth</a> used the terms <i>Britannia minor</i> and <i>Britannia major</i> to distinguish Brittany from Britain.\n</p><p>Breton-speaking people may pronounce the word <i>Breizh</i> in two different ways, according to their region of origin. Breton can be divided into two main dialects: the <i>KLT</i> (<a href="/wiki/Cornouaille" title="Cornouaille">Kerne</a>-Leon-<a href="/wiki/Tr%C3%A9gor" title="Tr\xc3\xa9gor">Tregor</a>) and the dialect of <a href="/wiki/Vannes" title="Vannes">Vannes</a>. KLT speakers pronounce it <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Breton" title="Help:IPA/Breton">[br\xc9\x9bjs]</a></span> and would write it <i>Breiz</i>, while the Vannetais speakers pronounce it <small></small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Breton" title="Help:IPA/Breton">[br\xc9\x9b\xcf\x87]</a></span> and would write it <i>Breih</i>. The official spelling is a compromise between both variants, with a <i>z</i> and an <i>h</i> together. In 1941, efforts to unify the dialects led to the creation of the so-called <i>Breton zh</i>, a standard which has never been widely accepted.<sup id="cite_ref-Walter_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Walter-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> On its side, <a href="/wiki/Gallo_language" title="Gallo language">Gallo language</a> has never had a widely accepted writing system and several ones coexist. For instance, the name of the region in that language can be written <i>Berta\xc3\xa8yn</i> in <i>ELG</i> script, or <i>Bert\xc3\xa8gn</i> in <i>MOGA</i>, and a couple of other scripts also exist.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Brittany" title="History of Brittany">History of Brittany</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistoric_origins">Prehistoric origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistoric origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:4735.1099_Menhire,bis_zu_4_Meter_hoch,von_OstnachWest_in_1167_Meter_Langen_Alignements(Granit-Steinreihen)_in_einem_Halbkreis_endend_Le_M%C3%A9nec,Carnac_,Departement_Morbihan,Bretagne_Steffen_Heilfort.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/4735.1099_Menhire%2Cbis_zu_4_Meter_hoch%2Cvon_OstnachWest_in_1167_Meter_Langen_Alignements%28Granit-Steinreihen%29_in_einem_Halbkreis_endend_Le_M%C3%A9nec%2CCarnac_%2CDepartement_Morbihan%2CBretagne_Steffen_Heilfort.JPG/220px-thumbnail.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/4735.1099_Menhire%2Cbis_zu_4_Meter_hoch%2Cvon_OstnachWest_in_1167_Meter_Langen_Alignements%28Granit-Steinreihen%29_in_einem_Halbkreis_endend_Le_M%C3%A9nec%2CCarnac_%2CDepartement_Morbihan%2CBretagne_Steffen_Heilfort.JPG/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/4735.1099_Menhire%2Cbis_zu_4_Meter_hoch%2Cvon_OstnachWest_in_1167_Meter_Langen_Alignements%28Granit-Steinreihen%29_in_einem_Halbkreis_endend_Le_M%C3%A9nec%2CCarnac_%2CDepartement_Morbihan%2CBretagne_Steffen_Heilfort.JPG/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:4735.1099_Menhire,bis_zu_4_Meter_hoch,von_OstnachWest_in_1167_Meter_Langen_Alignements(Granit-Steinreihen)_in_einem_Halbkreis_endend_Le_M%C3%A9nec,Carnac_,Departement_Morbihan,Bretagne_Steffen_Heilfort.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Carnac_stones" title="Carnac stones">Carnac stones</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Brittany has been inhabited by humans since the <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">Lower Paleolithic</a>. The first settlers were <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">Neanderthals</a>. This population was scarce and very similar to the other Neanderthals found in the whole of Western Europe. Their only original feature was a distinct culture, called "Colombanian".<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> One of the oldest <a href="/wiki/Hearth" title="Hearth">hearths</a> in the world has been found in <a href="/wiki/Plouhinec,_Finist%C3%A8re" title="Plouhinec, Finist\xc3\xa8re">Plouhinec, Finist\xc3\xa8re</a>. It is 450,000 years old.\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Homo_sapiens" title="Homo sapiens">Homo sapiens</a> settled in Brittany around 35,000 years ago. They replaced or absorbed the Neanderthals and developed local <a href="/wiki/Archaeological_industry" class="mw-redirect" title="Archaeological industry">industries</a>, similar to the <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2telperronian" title="Ch\xc3\xa2telperronian">Ch\xc3\xa2telperronian</a> or to the <a href="/wiki/Magdalenian" title="Magdalenian">Magdalenian</a>. After the <a href="/wiki/Last_glacial_period" title="Last glacial period">last glacial period</a>, the warmer climate allowed the area to become heavily wooded. At that time, Brittany was populated by relatively large communities who started to change their lifestyles from a life of hunting and gathering, to become settled farmers. Agriculture was introduced during the <a href="/wiki/5th_millennium_BC" title="5th millennium BC">5th millennium BC</a> by migrants from the south and east. However, the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">Neolithic Revolution</a> in Brittany did not happen due to a radical change of population, but by slow immigration and exchange of skills.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Neolithic Brittany is characterised by important <a href="/wiki/Megalithic_architectural_elements" title="Megalithic architectural elements">megalithic production</a>, and it is sometimes designated as the "core area" of megalithic culture.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The oldest monuments, <a href="/wiki/Cairn" title="Cairn">cairns</a>, were followed by princely tombs and <a href="/wiki/Stone_row" title="Stone row">stone rows</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Morbihan" title="Morbihan">Morbihan</a> <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partement</a></i>, on the southern coast, comprises a large share of these structures, including the <a href="/wiki/Carnac_stones" title="Carnac stones">Carnac stones</a> and the Broken Menhir of Er Grah in the <a href="/wiki/Locmariaquer_megaliths" title="Locmariaquer megaliths">Locmariaquer megaliths</a>, the largest single stone erected by Neolithic people.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallic_era">Gallic era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Gallic era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peuples_celtes_en_armorique.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Peuples_celtes_en_armorique.jpg/220px-Peuples_celtes_en_armorique.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Peuples_celtes_en_armorique.jpg/330px-Peuples_celtes_en_armorique.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Peuples_celtes_en_armorique.jpg/440px-Peuples_celtes_en_armorique.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="526" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peuples_celtes_en_armorique.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The five Gallic tribes of Brittany.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Protohistory" title="Protohistory">protohistorical period</a>, Brittany was inhabited by five Celtic tribes:<sup id="cite_ref-VenceslasKruta_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VenceslasKruta-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Curiosolitae" title="Curiosolitae">Curiosolitae</a>, who lived around the present town of <a href="/wiki/Corseul" title="Corseul">Corseul</a>. Their territory encompassed parts of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4tes-d%27Armor" title="C\xc3\xb4tes-d&#39;Armor">C\xc3\xb4tes-d\'Armor</a>, Ille-et-Vilaine and <a href="/wiki/Morbihan" title="Morbihan">Morbihan</a> <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partements</a></i>.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Namnetes" title="Namnetes">Namnetes</a>, who lived in the current <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">Loire-Atlantique</a> <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partement</a></i> (in today\'s administrative <i>r\xc3\xa9gion</i> of <a href="/wiki/Pays_de_la_Loire" title="Pays de la Loire">Pays de la Loire</a>), north of the <a href="/wiki/Loire_(river)" class="mw-redirect" title="Loire (river)">Loire</a>. They gave their name to the city of <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>. The south bank of the river was occupied by an allied tribe, the Ambilatres,<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> whose existence and territory remain unsure.<sup id="cite_ref-VenceslasKruta_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-VenceslasKruta-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Osismii" title="Osismii">Osismii</a>, who lived in the western part of Brittany. Their territory comprised the <a href="/wiki/Finist%C3%A8re" title="Finist\xc3\xa8re">Finist\xc3\xa8re</a> <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partement</a></i> and the western extremity of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4tes-d%27Armor" title="C\xc3\xb4tes-d&#39;Armor">C\xc3\xb4tes-d\'Armor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Morbihan" title="Morbihan">Morbihan</a>.</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Redones" class="mw-redirect" title="Redones">Redones</a> (or <i>Rhedones</i>), who lived in the eastern part of the <a href="/wiki/Ille-et-Vilaine" title="Ille-et-Vilaine">Ille-et-Vilaine</a> <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partement</a></i>. They gave their name to the city of <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a> (<i>Roazhon</i> in Breton language, in the center of the d\xc3\xa9partement) and to the town of <a href="/wiki/Redon" class="mw-redirect" title="Redon">Redon</a> (in the south of the <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>, bordering the <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i> of <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">Loire-Atlantique</a> in the administrative <i>r\xc3\xa9gion</i> of <a href="/wiki/Pays_de_la_Loire" title="Pays de la Loire">Pays de la Loire</a>, where its suburb town of <a href="/wiki/Saint-Nicolas-de-Redon" title="Saint-Nicolas-de-Redon">Saint-Nicolas-de-Redon</a> is located; however the city of Redon was founded around AD 832 under the initial name of <i>Riedones</i>, long after the <i>Redones</i> people were assimilated to Bretons&#160;; the cultural link between <i>Riedones</i> and the former <i>Redones</i> people is highly probable but difficult to recover and the name of <i>Riedones</i> may have been written from a local usage preserving the name of the former people in the vernacular oral language from a reading of an ancient Greek othography).</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Veneti_(Gaul)" title="Veneti (Gaul)">Veneti</a>, who lived in the present <a href="/wiki/Morbihan" title="Morbihan">Morbihan</a> <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partement</a></i> and gave their name to the city of <a href="/wiki/Vannes" title="Vannes">Vannes</a>. Despite confusion by the classical scholar <a href="/wiki/Strabo" title="Strabo">Strabo</a>, they were unrelated to the <a href="/wiki/Adriatic_Veneti" title="Adriatic Veneti">Adriatic Veneti</a>.</li></ul>\n<p>Those people had strong economic ties to the <a href="/wiki/Insular_Celts" title="Insular Celts">Insular Celts</a>, especially for the <a href="/wiki/Tin" title="Tin">tin</a> trade. Several tribes also belonged to an "Armorican <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a>" which, according to <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>, gathered the <a href="/wiki/Curiosolitae" title="Curiosolitae">Curiosolitae</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Redones" class="mw-redirect" title="Redones">Redones</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Osismii" title="Osismii">Osismii</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Unelli" title="Unelli">Unelli</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Caletes" title="Caletes">Caletes</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Lemovices" title="Lemovices">Lemovices</a> and the Ambibarii.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> The last four peoples mentioned by Caesar were respectively located in <a href="/wiki/Cotentin" class="mw-redirect" title="Cotentin">Cotentin</a> (Lower-Normandy), <a href="/wiki/Pays_de_Caux" title="Pays de Caux">pays de Caux</a> (Upper-Normandy), <a href="/wiki/Limousin" title="Limousin">Limousin</a> (Aquitany) and the location of the Ambibarii is unknown. The Caletes are sometimes also considered as Belgians and \xe2\x80\xb3Lemovices\xe2\x80\xb3 is probably a mistake for \xe2\x80\xb3<a href="/wiki/Lexovii" title="Lexovii">Lexovii</a>\xe2\x80\xb3 (Lower-Normandy).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gallo-Roman_era">Gallo-Roman era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Gallo-Roman era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Corseul_-_Temple_de_Mars_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Corseul_-_Temple_de_Mars_03.jpg/150px-Corseul_-_Temple_de_Mars_03.jpg" width="150" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Corseul_-_Temple_de_Mars_03.jpg/225px-Corseul_-_Temple_de_Mars_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Corseul_-_Temple_de_Mars_03.jpg/300px-Corseul_-_Temple_de_Mars_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="3008" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Corseul_-_Temple_de_Mars_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The temple of Mars in <a href="/wiki/Corseul" title="Corseul">Corseul</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The region became part of the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Republic" title="Roman Republic">Roman Republic</a> in 51 BC. It was included in the province of <a href="/wiki/Gallia_Lugdunensis" title="Gallia Lugdunensis">Gallia Lugdunensis</a> in 13 BC. Gallic towns and villages were redeveloped according to Roman standards, and several cities were created. These cities are Condate (<a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a>), Vorgium (<a href="/wiki/Carhaix" class="mw-redirect" title="Carhaix">Carhaix</a>), Darioritum (<a href="/wiki/Vannes" title="Vannes">Vannes</a>) and Condevincum or Condevicnum (<a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>). Together with Fanum Martis (<a href="/wiki/Corseul" title="Corseul">Corseul</a>), they were the capitals of the local <a href="/wiki/Civitas" title="Civitas">civitates</a>. They all had a <a href="/wiki/Grid_plan" title="Grid plan">grid plan</a> and a <a href="/wiki/Forum_(Roman)" title="Forum (Roman)">forum</a>, and sometimes a temple, a <a href="/wiki/Basilica" title="Basilica">basilica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thermae" title="Thermae">thermae</a> or an <a href="/wiki/Aqueduct_(water_supply)" title="Aqueduct (water supply)">aqueduct</a>, like <a href="/wiki/Carhaix" class="mw-redirect" title="Carhaix">Carhaix</a>. The Romans also built three major roads through the region. However, most of the population remained rural. The free peasants lived in small huts, whereas the landowners and their employees lived in proper <a href="/wiki/Villa_rustica" title="Villa rustica">villae rusticae</a>. The Gallic deities continued to be worshiped, and were often assimilated to the Roman gods. Only a small number of statues depicting Roman gods were found in Brittany, and most of the time they combine Celtic elements.<sup id="cite_ref-roman_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roman-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the 3rd century AD, the region was attacked several times by <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Franks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alamanni" class="mw-redirect" title="Alamanni">Alamanni</a> and pirates. At the same time, the local economy collapsed and many farming estates were abandoned. To face the invasions, many towns and cities were fortified, like <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vannes" title="Vannes">Vannes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-roman_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roman-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:France_Pays_bretons_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/France_Pays_bretons_map.svg/300px-France_Pays_bretons_map.svg.png" width="300" height="230" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/France_Pays_bretons_map.svg/450px-France_Pays_bretons_map.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/France_Pays_bretons_map.svg/600px-France_Pays_bretons_map.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="946" data-file-height="724" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:France_Pays_bretons_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> map of the traditional regions of Brittany in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_France" title="Kingdom of France">Ancien R\xc3\xa9gime France</a>. The earlier state of <a href="/wiki/Domnonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Domnonia">Domnonia</a> or <a href="/wiki/Domnon%C3%A9e" title="Domnon\xc3\xa9e">Domnon\xc3\xa9e</a> that united Brittany comprised the counties along the north coast.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Immigration_of_Britons">Immigration of Britons</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Immigration of Britons">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Toward the end of the 4th century, the <a href="/wiki/Britons_(historical)" class="mw-redirect" title="Britons (historical)">Britons</a> of what is now Wales and the <a href="/wiki/South_West_Peninsula" title="South West Peninsula">South-Western peninsula of Great Britain</a> began to emigrate to <a href="/wiki/Armorica" title="Armorica">Armorica</a>. The history behind such an establishment is unclear, but medieval Breton, Angevin and Welsh sources connect it to a figure known as <a href="/wiki/Conan_Meriadoc" title="Conan Meriadoc">Conan Meriadoc</a>. Welsh literary sources assert that Conan came to Armorica on the orders of the Roman usurper <a href="/wiki/Magnus_Maximus" title="Magnus Maximus">Magnus Maximus</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> who sent some of his British troops to Gaul to enforce his claims and settled them in Armorica. This account was supported by the Counts of Anjou, who claimed descent from a Roman soldier<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> expelled from Lower Brittany by Conan on Magnus\'s orders. Regardless of the truth of this story, Brythonic (British Celtic) settlement probably increased during the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Saxon_invasion_of_Britain" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglo-Saxon invasion of Britain">Anglo-Saxon invasion of Britain</a> in the 5th and 6th centuries. Scholars such as <a href="/wiki/L%C3%A9on_Fleuriot" title="L\xc3\xa9on Fleuriot">L\xc3\xa9on Fleuriot</a> have suggested a two-wave model of migration from Britain which saw the emergence of an independent Breton people and established the dominance of the <a href="/wiki/Brittonic_languages" title="Brittonic languages">Brythonic</a> <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton language</a> in Armorica.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Their <a href="/wiki/Petty_kingdom" title="Petty kingdom">petty kingdoms</a> are now known by the names of the French counties that succeeded them&#8212;<a href="/wiki/Domnon%C3%A9e" title="Domnon\xc3\xa9e">Domnon\xc3\xa9e</a> (<a href="/wiki/Devon" title="Devon">Devon</a>), <a href="/wiki/Cornouaille" title="Cornouaille">Cornouaille</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cornwall" title="Cornwall">Cornwall</a>), <a href="/wiki/Viscounty_of_L%C3%A9on" title="Viscounty of L\xc3\xa9on">L\xc3\xa9on</a> (<a href="/wiki/Caerleon" title="Caerleon">Caerleon</a>); but these names in Breton and <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> are in most cases identical to their British homelands. (In Breton and French, however, <a href="/wiki/Gwened_(kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gwened (kingdom)">Gwened</a> or <a href="/wiki/Pays_Vannetais" class="mw-redirect" title="Pays Vannetais">Vannetais</a> continued the name of the indigenous <a href="/wiki/Veneti_(Gauls)" class="mw-redirect" title="Veneti (Gauls)">Veneti</a>.) Although the details remain confused, these colonies consisted of related and intermarried dynasties which repeatedly unified (as by the 7th-century <a href="/wiki/Saint_Judica%C3%ABl" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Judica\xc3\xabl">Saint Judica\xc3\xabl</a>) before splintering again according to Celtic inheritance practices. The area was finally consolidated in the 840s under <a href="/wiki/Nominoe" title="Nominoe">Nominoe</a> in resistance to <a href="/wiki/Franks" title="Franks">Frankish</a> control.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Among the immigrant Britons, there were some clergymen who helped the <a href="/wiki/Evangelisation" class="mw-redirect" title="Evangelisation">evangelisation</a> of the region, which was still pagan, particularly in rural areas.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Britonia6hcentury.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Britonia6hcentury.png/220px-Britonia6hcentury.png" width="220" height="386" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Britonia6hcentury.png/330px-Britonia6hcentury.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f9/Britonia6hcentury.png/440px-Britonia6hcentury.png 2x" data-file-width="1670" data-file-height="2928" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Britonia6hcentury.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Brythonic_languages" class="mw-redirect" title="Brythonic languages">Brythonic</a> community around the 6th century. The sea was a communication medium rather than a barrier.</div></div></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_the_Catalaunian_Plains">Battle of the Catalaunian Plains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Battle of the Catalaunian Plains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The army recruited for <a href="/wiki/Flavius_Aetius" title="Flavius Aetius">Flavius Aetius</a> to combat <a href="/wiki/Attila_the_Hun" class="mw-redirect" title="Attila the Hun">Attila the Hun</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Catalaunian_Plains" title="Battle of the Catalaunian Plains">Battle of the Catalaunian Plains</a> included Romans, Visigoths, Franks, Alans and Armoricans, amongst others.  The Alans were placed front and centre, opposite the Huns.  The Armoricans supplied archers who attacked the Huns\' front lines during the main battle and thwarted Attila\'s night assault on the Roman camp with a hail of arrows "like rain".  After the battle was won, Aetius sent the Alans to Armorica and Galicia.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Riothamus">Riothamus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Riothamus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The late 5th century Brittonic leader <a href="/wiki/Riothamus" title="Riothamus">Riothamus</a> received correspondence from the eminent Roman jurist <a href="/wiki/Sidonius_Apollinaris" title="Sidonius Apollinaris">Sidonius Apollinaris</a> and was called "King of the Britons" by <a href="/wiki/Jordanes" title="Jordanes">Jordanes</a>.  Some suggest that he was a Breton, though others believe that he was from Britain, pointing to the passage that he arrived in the land of the Biturges "by way of Ocean", which would hardly have been efficient or required for a Breton.  Both historians describe Riothamus\'s losing battle against King <a href="/wiki/Euric" title="Euric">Euric</a> of the Visigoths at <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9ols" title="D\xc3\xa9ols">D\xc3\xa9ols</a> around the year 470.  In response to a plea from the Roman Emperor <a href="/wiki/Anthemius" title="Anthemius">Anthemius</a>, Riothamus had led twelve thousand men to establish a military presence in <a href="/wiki/Bourges" title="Bourges">Bourges</a> in central Gaul, but was betrayed by <a href="/wiki/Arvandus" title="Arvandus">Arvandus</a>, the Praetorian Prefect of Gaul, and subsequently ambushed by Euric\'s army.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;c&#93;</a></sup> After a long battle, the Armorican survivors escaped to <a href="/wiki/Avallon" title="Avallon">Avallon</a> in <a href="/wiki/Burgundy" title="Burgundy">Burgundy</a>, after which they are lost to history.  According to Breton king-lists, Riotham survived and reigned as Prince of <a href="/wiki/Domnonia" class="mw-redirect" title="Domnonia">Domnonia</a> until his death sometime between 500 and 520, though this may have been a different person.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle_Ages">Middle Ages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Middle Ages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nominoe_triumphant.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Nominoe_triumphant.jpg/130px-Nominoe_triumphant.jpg" width="130" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Nominoe_triumphant.jpg/195px-Nominoe_triumphant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Nominoe_triumphant.jpg/260px-Nominoe_triumphant.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1130" data-file-height="1331" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nominoe_triumphant.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A 1922 nationalist engraving of <a href="/wiki/Nominoe" title="Nominoe">Nominoe</a>, first king of Brittany.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_La_Roche-Derrien.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Battle_of_La_Roche-Derrien.jpg/170px-Battle_of_La_Roche-Derrien.jpg" width="170" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Battle_of_La_Roche-Derrien.jpg/255px-Battle_of_La_Roche-Derrien.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Battle_of_La_Roche-Derrien.jpg/340px-Battle_of_La_Roche-Derrien.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="672" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_La_Roche-Derrien.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_La_Roche-Derrien" title="Battle of La Roche-Derrien">Battle of Ar Roc\'h-Derrien</a> during the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Breton_Succession" title="War of the Breton Succession">War of the Breton Succession</a></div></div></div>\n<p>At the beginning of the medieval era, Brittany was divided between three kingdoms, <a href="/wiki/Domnon%C3%A9e" title="Domnon\xc3\xa9e">Domnonea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornouaille" title="Cornouaille">Cornouaille</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bro%C3%ABrec" class="mw-redirect" title="Bro\xc3\xabrec">Bro\xc3\xabrec</a>. These realms eventually merged into a single state during the 9th century.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-28">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> The unification of Brittany was carried out by <a href="/wiki/Nominoe" title="Nominoe">Nominoe</a>, king between 845 and 851 and considered as the Breton <i><a href="/wiki/Pater_Patriae" title="Pater Patriae">pater patriae</a></i>. His son <a href="/wiki/Erispoe" title="Erispoe">Erispoe</a> secured the independence of the new kingdom of Brittany and won the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jengland" title="Battle of Jengland">Battle of Jengland</a> against <a href="/wiki/Charles_the_Bald" title="Charles the Bald">Charles the Bald</a>. The Bretons won another war in 867, and the kingdom reached then its maximum extent: it received parts of <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maine_(province_of_France)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maine (province of France)">Maine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anjou" title="Anjou">Anjou</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a>.\n</p><p>Brittany was heavily attacked by the <a href="/wiki/Vikings" title="Vikings">Vikings</a> at the beginning of the 10th century. The kingdom lost its eastern territories, including <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">Normandy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anjou" title="Anjou">Anjou</a>, and the county of <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a> was given to <a href="/wiki/Fulk_I,_Count_of_Anjou" title="Fulk I, Count of Anjou">Fulk I of Anjou</a> in 909. However, Nantes was seized by the Vikings in 914, and was eventually liberated by <a href="/wiki/Alan_II,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Alan II, Duke of Brittany">Alan II of Brittany</a> in 937 with the support of his god-brother King <a href="/wiki/%C3%86thelstan" title="\xc3\x86thelstan">\xc3\x86thelstan</a> of England. Alan II totally expelled the Vikings from Brittany and recreated a strong Breton state. He paid homage to <a href="/wiki/Louis_IV_of_France" title="Louis IV of France">Louis IV of France</a> (who was \xc3\x86thelstan\'s nephew and had returned from England in the same year as Alan II) and thus Brittany ceased to be a kingdom and became a duchy.\n</p><p>Several Breton lords helped <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">William the Conqueror</a> to invade England and received large estates there (e.g. William\'s double-second cousin <a href="/wiki/Alan_Rufus" title="Alan Rufus">Alan Rufus</a> and the latter\'s brother <a href="/wiki/Brian_of_Brittany" title="Brian of Brittany">Brian of Brittany</a>). Some of these lords were powerful rivals. Medieval Brittany was far from being a united nation. The French king maintained envoys in Brittany, alliances contracted by local lords often overlapped and there was no specific Breton consciousness. For example, Brittany replaced <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> with French as its official language in the 13th century, 300 years before France did so itself, and the <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton language</a> never had any formal status. The <a href="/wiki/Foreign_policy" title="Foreign policy">foreign policy</a> of the duchy changed many times; the dukes were usually independent but they often contracted alliances with England or France. Their support for each nation became very important during the 14th century, because the English kings then started to claim the French throne.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Breton_War_of_Succession" class="mw-redirect" title="Breton War of Succession">Breton War of Succession</a>, a local episode of the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years&#39; War">Hundred Years\' War</a>, saw the House of <a href="/wiki/Blois" title="Blois">Blois</a>, backed by the French, fighting with the House of <a href="/wiki/Montfort_of_Brittany" title="Montfort of Brittany">Montfort</a>, backed by the English. The Montforts won in 1364 and enjoyed a period of total independence until the end of the Hundred Years\' War, because France was weakened and stopped sending royal envoys to the Court of Brittany.  English diplomatic failures led to the Breton cavalry commanders Arthur, Comte de Richemont (later to become <a href="/wiki/Arthur_III,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Arthur III, Duke of Brittany">Arthur III, Duke of Brittany</a>) and his nephew <a href="/wiki/Peter_II,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Peter II, Duke of Brittany">Peter II, Duke of Brittany</a> playing key roles on the French side during the deciding stages of the War (the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Patay" title="Battle of Patay">Battle of Patay</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Arras_(1435)" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Arras (1435)">Treaty of Arras (1435)</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Formigny" title="Battle of Formigny">Battle of Formigny</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Castillon" title="Battle of Castillon">Battle of Castillon</a>).  However, Brittany lost the <a href="/wiki/Mad_War" title="Mad War">Mad War</a> against France in 1488, mostly because of its internal divisions which were exacerbated by the corruption at the court of <a href="/wiki/Francis_II,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Francis II, Duke of Brittany">Francis II, Duke of Brittany</a>. Indeed, some Breton lords were fighting on the French side.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Union_with_the_French_Crown_and_modern_period">Union with the French Crown and modern period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Union with the French Crown and modern period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Brittany_and_France" title="Union of Brittany and France">Union of Brittany and France</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Anne_de_bretagne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Anne_de_bretagne.jpg/170px-Anne_de_bretagne.jpg" width="170" height="217" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Anne_de_bretagne.jpg/255px-Anne_de_bretagne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Anne_de_bretagne.jpg/340px-Anne_de_bretagne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Anne_de_bretagne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Brittany" title="Anne of Brittany">Anne of Brittany</a> is regarded in Brittany as a conscientious ruler who defended the duchy against France.</div></div></div>\n<p>After the <a href="/wiki/Mad_War" title="Mad War">Mad War</a>, the duke <a href="/wiki/Francis_II_of_Brittany" class="mw-redirect" title="Francis II of Brittany">Francis II</a> could not marry off his daughter <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Brittany" title="Anne of Brittany">Anne</a> without the King of France\'s consent. Nonetheless, she married the <a href="/wiki/Maximilian_I,_Holy_Roman_Emperor" title="Maximilian I, Holy Roman Emperor">Holy Roman Emperor</a> in 1490, but this led to a severe crisis with France. <a href="/wiki/Charles_VIII_of_France" title="Charles VIII of France">Charles VIII of France</a> besieged <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a> and had the marriage cancelled. He eventually married <a href="/wiki/Anne_of_Brittany" title="Anne of Brittany">Anne of Brittany</a>. After he died childless, the duchess had to marry his heir and cousin <a href="/wiki/Louis_XII_of_France" title="Louis XII of France">Louis XII</a>. Anne unsuccessfully tried to preserve Breton independence, but she died in 1514 and the union between the two crowns was formally carried out by <a href="/wiki/Francis_I_of_France" title="Francis I of France">Francis I</a> in 1532. He granted several privileges to Brittany, such as exemption from the <a href="/wiki/Gabelle" title="Gabelle">gabelle</a>, a tax on salt which was very unpopular in France.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>  Under the <a href="/wiki/Ancien_R%C3%A9gime" title="Ancien R\xc3\xa9gime">Ancien R\xc3\xa9gime</a>, Brittany and France were governed as separate countries under the same crown, so Breton aristocrats in the French <a href="/wiki/Court_(royal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Court (royal)">royal court</a> were classed as <a href="/wiki/Prince_%C3%A9tranger" title="Prince \xc3\xa9tranger">Princes \xc3\xa9trangers</a> (foreign princes).\n</p><p>From the 15th to the 18th century, Brittany reached an economic golden age.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;d&#93;</a></sup> The region was located on the seaways between Spain, England and the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and it greatly benefited from the creation of a <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">French colonial empire</a>. Local seaports like <a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Brieuc" title="Saint-Brieuc">Saint-Brieuc</a> quickly expanded, and <a href="/wiki/Lorient" title="Lorient">Lorient</a>, first spelled "L\'Orient", was founded in the 17th century. <a href="/wiki/Saint-Malo" title="Saint-Malo">Saint-Malo</a> was then known for its <a href="/wiki/French_corsairs" title="French corsairs">corsairs</a>, Brest was a major base for the <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">French Navy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a> flourished with the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_slave_trade" title="Atlantic slave trade">Atlantic slave trade</a>. On its side, the inland provided <a href="/wiki/Hemp" title="Hemp">hemp</a> ropes and canvas and <a href="/wiki/Linen" title="Linen">linen</a> sheets. However, <a href="/wiki/Colbertism" title="Colbertism">Colbertism</a>, which encouraged the creation of many factories, did not favour the Breton industry because most of the royal factories were opened in other provinces. Moreover, several conflicts between France and England led the latter to restrain its trade, and the Breton economy went into recession during the 18th century.\n</p><p>Two significant revolts occurred in the 17th and 18th centuries: the <a href="/wiki/Revolt_of_the_papier_timbr%C3%A9" title="Revolt of the papier timbr\xc3\xa9">Revolt of the papier timbr\xc3\xa9</a> (1675) and the <a href="/wiki/Pontcallec_Conspiracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontcallec Conspiracy">Pontcallec Conspiracy</a> (1719). Both arose from attempts to resist centralisation and assert Breton constitutional exceptions to tax.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many Bretons crossed the Atlantic to support the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American War of Independence</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> These included many sailors such as <a href="/wiki/Armand_de_Kersaint" title="Armand de Kersaint">Armand de Kersaint</a> and soldiers such as <a href="/wiki/Charles_Armand_Tuffin,_marquis_de_la_Rouerie" title="Charles Armand Tuffin, marquis de la Rouerie">Charles Armand Tuffin, marquis de la Rouerie</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_1789">Since 1789</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Since 1789">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A9volte_Fouesnant.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/R%C3%A9volte_Fouesnant.jpg/220px-R%C3%A9volte_Fouesnant.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/R%C3%A9volte_Fouesnant.jpg/330px-R%C3%A9volte_Fouesnant.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/R%C3%A9volte_Fouesnant.jpg/440px-R%C3%A9volte_Fouesnant.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="1152" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:R%C3%A9volte_Fouesnant.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The mutineers of <a href="/wiki/Fouesnant" title="Fouesnant">Fouesnant</a> arrested by the National Guard of <a href="/wiki/Quimper" title="Quimper">Quimper</a> in 1792.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Duchy was legally abolished during the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, in 1789, and divided into five <a href="/wiki/Departments_of_France" title="Departments of France">departments</a>. Brittany also lost all its privileges. Three years later, the area became a centre of <a href="/wiki/Royalist" title="Royalist">royalist</a> and Catholic resistance to the Revolution during the <a href="/wiki/Chouannerie" title="Chouannerie">Chouannerie</a>. During the 19th century, Brittany remained in economic recession, and many Bretons emigrated to other French regions, particularly to Paris. This trend remained strong until the beginning of the 20th century. Nonetheless, the region was also modernising, with new roads and railways being built, and some places being industrialised. <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a> specialised in <a href="/wiki/Shipbuilding" title="Shipbuilding">shipbuilding</a> and food processing (sugar, exotic fruits and vegetables, fish...), <a href="/wiki/Foug%C3%A8res" title="Foug\xc3\xa8res">Foug\xc3\xa8res</a> in glass and shoe production, and <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">metallurgy</a> was practised in small towns such as <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teaubriant" title="Ch\xc3\xa2teaubriant">Ch\xc3\xa2teaubriant</a> and <a href="/wiki/Inzinzac-Lochrist" title="Inzinzac-Lochrist">Lochrist</a>, known for its <a href="/wiki/Labour_movement" title="Labour movement">labour movements</a>.\n</p><p>The region remained deeply Catholic, and during the <a href="/wiki/Second_French_Empire" title="Second French Empire">Second Empire</a>, the conservative values were strongly reasserted. When the Republic was re-established in 1871, there were rumours that Breton troops were mistrusted and mistreated at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Conlie" title="Camp Conlie">Camp Conlie</a> during the <a href="/wiki/Franco-Prussian_War" title="Franco-Prussian War">Franco-Prussian War</a> because of fears that they were a threat to the Republic.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RAF_attack_Saint_Malo_31_Jul_1942.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/RAF_attack_Saint_Malo_31_Jul_1942.jpg/220px-RAF_attack_Saint_Malo_31_Jul_1942.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/RAF_attack_Saint_Malo_31_Jul_1942.jpg/330px-RAF_attack_Saint_Malo_31_Jul_1942.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/RAF_attack_Saint_Malo_31_Jul_1942.jpg/440px-RAF_attack_Saint_Malo_31_Jul_1942.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3731" data-file-height="2821" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RAF_attack_Saint_Malo_31_Jul_1942.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">Royal Air Force</a> attack on <a href="/wiki/Saint-Malo" title="Saint-Malo">Saint-Malo</a> in 1942.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the 19th century, the <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton language</a> started to decline precipitously, mainly because of the <a href="/wiki/Francization" title="Francization">Francization</a> policy conducted under the <a href="/wiki/Third_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Third French Republic">Third Republic</a>. On one hand, children <a href="/wiki/Vergonha" title="Vergonha">were not allowed to speak Breton at school, and were punished by teachers if they did.</a> Famously, signs in schools read: "It is forbidden to speak Breton and to spit on the floor" ("Il est interdit de parler Breton et de cracher par terre").<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On the other hand, Breton (like Latin) was considered as a language that kept Brittany in the hands of the Roman Catholic church and learning French was a way, especially for women, to free themselves from the influence of the church.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amoco_Cadiz_1_edit1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Amoco_Cadiz_1_edit1.jpg/220px-Amoco_Cadiz_1_edit1.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Amoco_Cadiz_1_edit1.jpg/330px-Amoco_Cadiz_1_edit1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Amoco_Cadiz_1_edit1.jpg/440px-Amoco_Cadiz_1_edit1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2544" data-file-height="1696" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amoco_Cadiz_1_edit1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Amoco_Cadiz_oil_spill" title="Amoco Cadiz oil spill">Amoco Cadiz oil spill</a> in 1978 deeply marked Breton people.</div></div></div>\n<p>At the same time, the <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Revival" title="Celtic Revival">Celtic Revival</a> led to the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Breton_Regionalist_Union" title="Breton Regionalist Union">Breton Regionalist Union</a> (URB) and later to independence movements linked to Irish, Welsh and Scottish independence parties in the UK and to <a href="/wiki/Pan-Celticism" title="Pan-Celticism">pan-Celticism</a>. However, the audience of these movements remained very low and their ideas did not reach a large public until the 20th century. The <a href="/wiki/Seiz_Breur" title="Seiz Breur">Seiz Breur</a> movement, created in 1923, permitted a Breton artistic revival<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> but its ties with <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazism</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Collaborationism" title="Collaborationism">collaborationism</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Breton_National_Party" title="Breton National Party">Breton National Party</a> during World War II weakened Breton nationalism in the post-war period.\n</p><p>Brittany lost 240,000 men during the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> was also catastrophic for the region. It was invaded by <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a> in 1940 and freed after <a href="/wiki/Operation_Cobra" title="Operation Cobra">Operation Cobra</a> in August 1944. However, the areas around <a href="/wiki/Saint-Nazaire" title="Saint-Nazaire">Saint-Nazaire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lorient" title="Lorient">Lorient</a> only surrendered on 10 and 11 May 1945, several days after the German capitulation. The two port towns had been virtually destroyed by Allied air raids, like <a href="/wiki/Brest,_France" title="Brest, France">Brest</a> and <a href="/wiki/Saint-Malo" title="Saint-Malo">Saint-Malo</a>, and other towns, such as <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a>, had also suffered.\n</p><p>In 1956, Brittany was legally reconstituted as the <a href="/wiki/Brittany_(administrative_region)" title="Brittany (administrative region)">Region of Brittany</a>, although the region excluded the ducal capital of <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">surrounding area</a>. Nevertheless, Brittany retained its cultural distinctiveness, and a new cultural revival emerged during the 1960s and 1970s. Bilingual schools were opened, singers started to write songs in Breton, and ecological catastrophes such as the <a href="/wiki/Amoco_Cadiz_oil_spill" title="Amoco Cadiz oil spill">Amoco Cadiz oil spill</a> or the <a href="/wiki/MV_Erika" title="MV Erika">Erika oil spill</a> and water pollution because of intensive pig farming favoured new movements to protect the natural heritage.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_France" title="Politics of France">Politics of France</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Traditional_subdivisions">Traditional subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Traditional subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Brittany as a political entity disappeared in 1790, when it was divided into five <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partements</a>. The Breton d\xc3\xa9partements more or less correspond to the nine Catholic <a href="/wiki/Diocese" title="Diocese">dioceses</a> that appeared at the beginning of the Middle Ages. They were often called "pays" or "bro" ("country" in French and <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a>) and they also served as fiscal and military districts.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> Brittany is also divided between <i><a href="/wiki/Lower_Brittany" title="Lower Brittany">Lower Brittany</a></i> ("Basse Bretagne" and "Breizh Izel"), corresponding to the western half, where <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a> is traditionally spoken, and <i><a href="/wiki/Upper_Brittany" title="Upper Brittany">Upper Brittany</a></i> ("Haute Bretagne" and "Breizh Uhel"), corresponding to the eastern half, where <a href="/wiki/Gallo_language" title="Gallo language">Gallo</a> is traditionally spoken. The historical Breton dioceses were:\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Upper_Brittany" title="Upper Brittany">Upper Brittany</a>:\n<ul><li>The <i>Pays nantais</i>, around <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, corresponding to the <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">Loire-Atlantique</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>.</li>\n<li>The <i>Pays rennais</i>, around <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a>, forming part of the <a href="/wiki/Ille-et-Vilaine" title="Ille-et-Vilaine">Ille-et-Vilaine</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>.</li>\n<li>The <i>Pays de Dol</i>, around <a href="/wiki/Dol-de-Bretagne" title="Dol-de-Bretagne">Dol-de-Bretagne</a>, corresponding to the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Ille-et-Vilaine" title="Ille-et-Vilaine">Ille-et-Vilaine</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>.</li>\n<li>The <i>Pays de Saint-Brieuc</i>, around <a href="/wiki/Saint-Brieuc" title="Saint-Brieuc">Saint-Brieuc</a>, forming part of the <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4tes-d%27Armor" title="C\xc3\xb4tes-d&#39;Armor">C\xc3\xb4tes-d\'Armor</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>.</li>\n<li>The <i>Pays de Saint-Malo</i>, around <a href="/wiki/Saint-Malo" title="Saint-Malo">Saint-Malo</a>, divided between <a href="/wiki/Ille-et-Vilaine" title="Ille-et-Vilaine">Ille-et-Vilaine</a>, C\xc3\xb4tes-d\'Armor and <a href="/wiki/Morbihan" title="Morbihan">Morbihan</a>.</li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lower_Brittany" title="Lower Brittany">Lower Brittany</a>:\n<ul><li>The <i>Pays vannetais</i>, around <a href="/wiki/Vannes" title="Vannes">Vannes</a>, corresponding to the <a href="/wiki/Morbihan" title="Morbihan">Morbihan</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>.</li>\n<li>The <i>Cornouaille</i>, around <a href="/wiki/Quimper" title="Quimper">Quimper</a>, divided between <a href="/wiki/Finist%C3%A8re" title="Finist\xc3\xa8re">Finist\xc3\xa8re</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4tes-d%27Armor" title="C\xc3\xb4tes-d&#39;Armor">C\xc3\xb4tes-d\'Armor</a>.</li>\n<li>The <i>L\xc3\xa9on</i>, around <a href="/wiki/Saint-Pol-de-L%C3%A9on" title="Saint-Pol-de-L\xc3\xa9on">Saint-Pol-de-L\xc3\xa9on</a>, corresponding to the northern part of the <a href="/wiki/Finist%C3%A8re" title="Finist\xc3\xa8re">Finist\xc3\xa8re</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>.</li>\n<li>The <i>Tr\xc3\xa9gor</i>, around <a href="/wiki/Tr%C3%A9guier" title="Tr\xc3\xa9guier">Tr\xc3\xa9guier</a>, forming part of the <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4tes-d%27Armor" title="C\xc3\xb4tes-d&#39;Armor">C\xc3\xb4tes-d\'Armor</a> <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>.</li></ul></li></ul>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, four dioceses were suppressed and the five remaining ones were modified to have the same administrative borders as the <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partements</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capital_cities">Capital cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Capital cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Nantes_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Nantes_3.jpg/220px-Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Nantes_3.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Nantes_3.jpg/330px-Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Nantes_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Nantes_3.jpg/440px-Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Nantes_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2304" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Nantes_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_des_ducs_de_Bretagne" title="Ch\xc3\xa2teau des ducs de Bretagne">ch\xc3\xa2teau des ducs de Bretagne</a> in <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, permanent residence of the last dukes.</div></div></div>\n<p>Brittany has several historical capital cities. When it was an independent duchy, the <a href="/wiki/Estates_of_Brittany" title="Estates of Brittany">Estates of Brittany</a>, which can be compared to a parliament, met in various towns: <a href="/wiki/Dinan" title="Dinan">Dinan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Plo%C3%ABrmel" title="Plo\xc3\xabrmel">Plo\xc3\xabrmel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Redon" class="mw-redirect" title="Redon">Redon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vitr%C3%A9,_Ille-et-Vilaine" title="Vitr\xc3\xa9, Ille-et-Vilaine">Vitr\xc3\xa9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A9rande" title="Gu\xc3\xa9rande">Gu\xc3\xa9rande</a>, and, most of all, <a href="/wiki/Vannes" title="Vannes">Vannes</a>, where they met 19 times, and <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, 17 times. The Court and the government were also very mobile, and each dynasty favoured its own castles and estates. The dukes mostly lived in <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vannes" title="Vannes">Vannes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Redon" class="mw-redirect" title="Redon">Redon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Foug%C3%A8res" title="Foug\xc3\xa8res">Foug\xc3\xa8res</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dol-de-Bretagne" title="Dol-de-Bretagne">Dol-de-Bretagne</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dinan" title="Dinan">Dinan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gu%C3%A9rande" title="Gu\xc3\xa9rande">Gu\xc3\xa9rande</a>. All these towns except Vannes are located in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Brittany" title="Upper Brittany">Upper Brittany</a>, thus not in the Breton speaking area.\n</p><p>Among all these towns, only <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vannes" title="Vannes">Vannes</a>, which were the biggest ones, could really pretend to the capital status. The dukes were crowned in Rennes and they had a large castle there; it was however destroyed during the 15th century. Vannes, on its side, was the seat of the Chamber of Accounts and of the Parliament until the union with France. The Parliament was then transferred to Rennes, and the Chamber of Accounts to Nantes. Nantes, nicknamed "the city of the Dukes of Brittany", was also the permanent residence of the last dukes. The <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_des_ducs_de_Bretagne" title="Ch\xc3\xa2teau des ducs de Bretagne">Ch\xc3\xa2teau des ducs de Bretagne</a> still stands in the city centre. Nowadays, <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a> is the only official capital of the <a href="/wiki/Brittany_(administrative_region)" title="Brittany (administrative region)">region of Brittany</a>. It is also the seat of an <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_province" title="Ecclesiastical province">ecclesiastical province</a> encompassing Brittany and the <a href="/wiki/Pays_de_la_Loire" title="Pays de la Loire">Pays de la Loire</a> region.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Present_subdivisions">Present subdivisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Present subdivisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_France" title="Administrative divisions of France">Administrative divisions of France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brittany_(administrative_region)" title="Brittany (administrative region)">Brittany (administrative region)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">Loire-Atlantique</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bretagne_historique_2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bretagne_historique_2.png/220px-Bretagne_historique_2.png" width="220" height="233" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bretagne_historique_2.png/330px-Bretagne_historique_2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Bretagne_historique_2.png/440px-Bretagne_historique_2.png 2x" data-file-width="526" data-file-height="556" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bretagne_historique_2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Brittany_(administrative_region)" title="Brittany (administrative region)">region Brittany</a> comprises four historical Breton <i>d\xc3\xa9partements</i>. <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">Loire-Atlantique</a>, in light blue, is part of the <a href="/wiki/Pays_de_la_Loire" title="Pays de la Loire">Pays de la Loire</a> region.</div></div></div>\n<p>During the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, Brittany was divided into five <i><a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="D\xc3\xa9partement">d\xc3\xa9partements</a></i>, each made up of three or four <i><a href="/wiki/Arrondissements_of_France" title="Arrondissements of France">arrondissements</a></i>. The arrondissements are further divided in <a href="/wiki/Cantons_of_France" title="Cantons of France">cantons</a>, which are themselves made up of one or several <a href="/wiki/Communes_of_France" title="Communes of France">communes</a>. The communes and the d\xc3\xa9partements have a local council elected by their citizens, but arrondissements and cantons are not run by elected officials. The cantons serve as an <a href="/wiki/Electoral" class="mw-redirect" title="Electoral">electoral</a> district for the election of the d\xc3\xa9partement councils and arrondissements are run by a subprefect appointed by the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the French Republic">French president</a>. The president also appoints a prefect in each d\xc3\xa9partement.\n</p><p>Because the d\xc3\xa9partements are small and numerous, the French government tried to create wider regions during the 20th century. For the Breton nationalists, it was an occasion to recreate Brittany as a political and administrative entity, but the new region had to be economically efficient. <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a> and its <i>d\xc3\xa9partement</i>, <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">Loire-Atlantique</a>, raised concerns because they were off-centered, more integrated with the <a href="/wiki/Loire_Valley" title="Loire Valley">Loire Valley</a> than with the Breton peninsula. The French government and local politicians also feared that <a href="/wiki/Nantes" title="Nantes">Nantes</a>, because of its population and its former Breton capital status, would have maintained a harmful competition with <a href="/wiki/Rennes" title="Rennes">Rennes</a> to get the regional institutions and investments.\n</p><p>Several drafts for French regions had been proposed since the 1920s, and the definitive regions were drawn in 1956. The new Brittany had four d\xc3\xa9partements, and <a href="/wiki/Loire-Atlantique" title="Loire-Atlantique">Loire-Atlantique</a> formed the <a href="/wiki/Pays_de_la_Loire" title="Pays de la Loire">Pays de la Loire</a> region together with parts of <a href="/wiki/Anjou" title="Anjou">Anjou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maine_(province_of_France)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maine (province of France)">Maine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Poitou" title="Poitou">Poitou</a>. In 1972, the regions received their present competencies, with an elected regional council. Since then, the <a href="/wiki/Brittany_(administrative_region)" title="Brittany (administrative region)">region of Brittany</a> has had its own <a href="/wiki/Regional_Council_of_Brittany" title="Regional Council of Brittany">council</a> and administrative bodies.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reunification">Reunification</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Brittany&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Reunification">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Bretagne_R%C3%A9unie" title="Bretagne R\xc3\xa9unie">Bretagne R\xc3\xa9unie</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bienvenue_en_Bretagne_historique.jpg" class="image"><img alt=""
